  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_43fff424-bd20-4b0f-82e9-6b97b0cc3851'
      });

      $('edition_8678711').observe('prototip:shown', function() {
        if (this.up('#box')) {
          $$('div.prototip').each(function(i){i.setStyle({zIndex: $('box').getStyle('z-index')})});

      newTip['wrapper'].addClassName('prototipAllowOverflow');

        $('edition_8678711').observe('prototip:shown', function () {
          $$('div.prototip').each(function (e) {
            if ($('edition_8678711').hasClassName('ignored')) {
              e.setStyle({'display': 'none'});
              return;
            }
            e.setStyle({'overflow': 'visible'});
          });

<span id="freeTextContainer5344058278716174764"><b>Review for this book is below the PSA. The PSA does not have anything to do with the book but a TOS policy change that Goodreads deemed not to tell their faithful users. </b><br/><br/><a href='http://s6.photobucket.com/user/veela-valoom/media/Goodreads_zpsfd34dfc1.jpg.html' target='_blank' rel='nofollow noopener'>

</a><br/><br/>This book started out strongly. Despite the protagonist being a brat (the throwing hissy fits kind) I was very into the story. However, when it got to the middle and she completely forgot about the family she loved because "ooooo cute boy" and the plot seemed to focus purely on her crushing on said boy they lost me. And the </span>
  <span id="freeText5344058278716174764" style="display:none"><b>Review for this book is below the PSA. The PSA does not have anything to do with the book but a TOS policy change that Goodreads deemed not to tell their faithful users. </b><br><br><a href="http://s6.photobucket.com/user/veela-valoom/media/Goodreads_zpsfd34dfc1.jpg.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380346370i/700802.jpg" alt=" photo Goodreads_zpsfd34dfc1.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>This book started out strongly. Despite the protagonist being a brat (the throwing hissy fits kind) I was very into the story. However, when it got to the middle and she completely forgot about the family she loved because "ooooo cute boy" and the plot seemed to focus purely on her crushing on said boy they lost me. And the overuse of the word "foxy" made me want to hit something. There was some SMASH BANG excitingness at the end but then it went into mopey melodramatic girl mode again.<br><br>SPOILERS BEYOND THIS POINT (BRIEF SPOILERS &amp; MINI RANT)<br><br>Seriously I can't stand when girls are like "Oh my relationships over I just want to die now." Nothing in books makes me ANGRIER. I've never called myself a feminist but this boy-centric female protagonist that is so common in paranormals makes me feel like one. It needs to stop! Girls should not lay down and hope to die just because a boy has left them. And it bothers me that women are the ones writing these weak female characters. </span>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1242703427?book_show_action=true">Apr 01, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Katerina" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Katerina" href="/user/show/5014021-katerina">Katerina</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781453688939" href="/book/show/8564935-switched">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5014021-katerina?shelf=paranormal">paranormal</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1242703427" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9091764942359994952">Sooo, after finishing <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/12180581.Switched__Trylle_Trilogy___1_' title='Switched (Trylle Trilogy, #1) by Amanda Hocking' rel='nofollow noopener'>Switched</a> I realized 2 things:<br/>1. I'm officially in love with <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/3486415.Amanda_Hocking' title='Amanda Hocking' rel='nofollow noopener'>Amanda Hocking</a><br/>2. Trolls are <i>
  <b>hot</b>
</i><br/>(3. I also suspect that I am a troll due to the hair thing, but I haven't found any proof yet. I'm looking on it.)<br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1442903588ra/16292092.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“Did you think you could treat me like shit at a dance, then sneak into my room in the middle of the night and tell me that I'm a troll with magical powers, and I'd just be like, yeah, that sounds right.” </i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br/>Wendy Everly, a girl whose mother tried to kill her </span>
  <span id="freeText9091764942359994952" style="display:none">Sooo, after finishing <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/12180581.Switched__Trylle_Trilogy___1_" title="Switched (Trylle Trilogy, #1) by Amanda Hocking" rel="nofollow noopener">Switched</a> I realized 2 things:<br>1. I'm officially in love with <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/3486415.Amanda_Hocking" title="Amanda Hocking" rel="nofollow noopener">Amanda Hocking</a><br>2. Trolls are <i>
  <b>hot</b>
</i><br>(3. I also suspect that I am a troll due to the hair thing, but I haven't found any proof yet. I'm looking on it.)<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1442903588ra/16292092.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“Did you think you could treat me like shit at a dance, then sneak into my room in the middle of the night and tell me that I'm a troll with magical powers, and I'd just be like, yeah, that sounds right.” </i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br>Wendy Everly, a girl whose mother tried to kill her when she was six and always thought that she was living someone else's life finds out that she <i>is</i> indeed living someone else's life, because she is a <b>changeling</b>, a child that is exchanged in secret for another child. Of course there is more, and she feels quite astonished when she is also told that she is a troll (although she isn't green), a royal one, the heir of the Trylle kingdom. So Wendy has to move into a palace with a cold mother when everyone prays for her downfall and another tribe wants to kidnap her for reasons unknown. And she has to fight her feelings for her sexy tracker/bodyguard, Finn.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1387448209ra/7597915.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>It is fun. It is so much fun. </b><br>This series is the reason why all my friends call me troll-lover, but I'm not particularly concerned because if Finn was <i>my</i> lover, <i>they</i> would be concerned. And jealous. *cue evil laughter*<br>I must admit I never thought I would want to be a troll or that a writer could make them such <b>interesting and fascinating creatures</b>, but Amanda did it! I loved the <b>fast pace</b> and the <b>mythology</b> and the <b>twists</b> in the story, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/12180581.Switched__Trylle_Trilogy___1_" title="Switched (Trylle Trilogy, #1) by Amanda Hocking" rel="nofollow noopener">Switched</a> was an easy and entertaining read that made me forget stupid reality and stupid reality stuff!<br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“I look at you because I can't look away Wendy.<br>That's kinda creepy.<br>I will work on being less creepy then.” </i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br>I found Wendy irritating most of the times because she kept on acting before thinking and she was quite immature, but there were signs of development, plus her life was not an easy one, so I'm giving her the benefit of doubt. But I can't understand why everyone is keeping her in the darkness! Wouldn't everything be easier if they just told her what she needed to know in order to acclimate to her new life and try harder to rule someday? Just saying! I liked Finn, but I don't like the way the things between them are heading,even though I enjoyed the tension. <b>Their love is not a healthy one.</b> Tove is becoming one of my favorite characters, and so are Willa, Matt and Rhys! Elora, well, I'm not that fond of her but I bet there is an explanation for her behavior!<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1465135169ra/19318915.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>To all paranormal fans all over the world, Trylle is an exciting world to dive in!!</b></span>
  <a data-text-id="9091764942359994952" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

  <span id="freeText4947956437886900886" style="display:none">A more formal (and better xD) review of this is available on <a href="http://wildheartbookblogs.blogspot.com/2012/03/review-switched-by-amanda-hocking.html" rel="nofollow noopener">my blog.</a> Check it out!<br /><br />_______________________________________<br /><br />I hadn't had a book infuriate me this much since <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/10429025.A_Beautiful_Dark__A_Beautiful_Dark___1_" title="A Beautiful Dark (A Beautiful Dark, #1) by Jocelyn Davies" rel="nofollow noopener">A Beautiful Dark</a>.<br /><br />So Wendy Everly finds out she's a changeling switched at birth, and that she's actually one of the Trylle─a.k.a. trolls. She's also a princess.<br /><br />Every. Single. Character. In this book. Expected her to know everything about Trylle life already. Nobody even educates this girl. Sometimes Finn, the hero, tries to, but then they end up making out or some other annoying romantic activity.<br /><br />Wendy was so damn unlikable. She was close to being a TSTL heroine. When her mother, Elora, yelled at her about the stupidest things, she just stood there and took it. She needs to learn to stand up for herself. -_-<br /><br />I would've probably liked her, or at least respected her more, if she would just stop letting that bitchy mother of hers to treat her like fecal matter.<br /><br />I didn't like the characters, the story, the romance, nothing. But a friend of mine told me that it gets better in the sequel. I do see some potential in this series, I guess.<br /><br />I'd probably still read the sequel, just to see if it really gets better. I mean, I got a copy of it already. I bought it at the same time I got this one. I guess I just had high hopes for this series. :/</span>

<div id="review_110996658" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/110996658" />
    <a title="Alex Bennett" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3010478-alex-bennett"><img alt="Alex Bennett" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1319413079p2/3010478.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/110996658?book_show_action=true">Jul 10, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Alex Bennett" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Alex Bennett" href="/user/show/3010478-alex-bennett">Alex Bennett</a>
      </span>

          added it


          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781250006318" href="/book/show/11457525-switched">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer110996658" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16880012819172715484"><b>Please check out <a href='http://www.electrifyingreviews.com/' rel='nofollow noopener'>Electrifying Reviews</a> for more reviews like this, plus giveaways, interviews, and more!</b><br/><br/>By now, practically everyone knows Amanda Hocking’s story. Self-published wonder turned multi-millionaire, now with multiple book deals. Before all of the hoopla, I read a little book called Switched. Even before all of the fame, I loved this book. So, of course, when it was re-released, I absolutely had to read it again. And let me tell you, I loved it even more this time around!<br/><br/>Switched is ex</span>
  <span id="freeText16880012819172715484" style="display:none"><b>Please check out <a href="http://www.electrifyingreviews.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">Electrifying Reviews</a> for more reviews like this, plus giveaways, interviews, and more!</b><br /><br />By now, practically everyone knows Amanda Hocking’s story. Self-published wonder turned multi-millionaire, now with multiple book deals. Before all of the hoopla, I read a little book called Switched. Even before all of the fame, I loved this book. So, of course, when it was re-released, I absolutely had to read it again. And let me tell you, I loved it even more this time around!<br /><br />Switched is extremely readable and entertaining. Both times I’ve read it, I’ve gotten pulled into the story immediately, and my eyes are glued to the pages until the book is done. The Trylle society is original and intricate, and I loved reading about the complexities of it, and how Wendy fits into all of it.<br /><br />Amanda Hocking has a smooth, exciting writing style. I’ve never read something by her I haven’t enjoyed immensely, even her blog posts! Her ability to create something so fun, yet thrilling in its own way is unique. I cannot wait to see where she goes in life, because I’m sure that her recent surge in popularity is not temporary.<br /><br />Wendy is a strong-willed girl, and reading Switched from her perspective was a joy. She is in a tough position, but she doesn’t budge when it comes to what she believes in, and I appreciate that. The other characters are completely enjoyable, and I loved them, and their interactions with each other.<br /><br />The Princess Diaries meets Tithe in Switched, the highly imaginative, immensely enjoyable novel from Amanda Hocking, an up-and-coming talent. I have nothing but love for Switched, and cannot wait to continue the story with Torn. </span>
  <a data-text-id="16880012819172715484" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_226979219" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/226979219" />
    <a title="Giselle" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4800103-giselle"><img alt="Giselle" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1310159877p2/4800103.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/226979219?book_show_action=true">Oct 24, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Giselle" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Giselle" href="/user/show/4800103-giselle">Giselle</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781250006318" href="/book/show/11457525-switched">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4800103-giselle?shelf=arc">arc</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4800103-giselle?shelf=own">own</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer226979219" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15671671030383892962">Trolls! I know, right? Flashy colorful hair, so-ugly-they're-cute dolls we all had at one point? In Amanda's world, these are all misconceptions. They're called Trylle, and they're beautiful, magical and on the brink of extinction. <br/><br/>With an entirely unique lore, Switched is able to stand out from all the other paranormal books available. I was fascinated by the Trylle mythology: How they lived, the monarchy, their custom of switching babies at birth. It was absolutely creative. Into this world co</span>
  <span id="freeText15671671030383892962" style="display:none">Trolls! I know, right? Flashy colorful hair, so-ugly-they're-cute dolls we all had at one point? In Amanda's world, these are all misconceptions. They're called Trylle, and they're beautiful, magical and on the brink of extinction. <br /><br />With an entirely unique lore, Switched is able to stand out from all the other paranormal books available. I was fascinated by the Trylle mythology: How they lived, the monarchy, their custom of switching babies at birth. It was absolutely creative. Into this world comes a collection of commendable characters that are both well developed and easily likeable - even a select few that are fun to hate. Wendy has a big personality. She's had a difficult, traumatic childhood, but that only made her stronger for the wear. She doesn't let anyone manipulate her. She's sympathetic and kind. All of which make her really relatable. I enjoyed going through her dilemmas with her. The stressful demands of becoming a princess overnight, the boy she's falling for- it was all delightful. Almost like a modern day fairy tale. <br /><br />Yes! The wonderful boys! From sweet to sweaty, Wendy has got more than her pick of lovely bachelors to chose from. I absolutely loved how the romance was played out in Switched. It's passionate and heartbreaking. It doesn't fall with the clichés of today's YA novels. It's unexpected - true to life. Truthfully, I devoured it and I can't fathom choosing a team. She can have them all, right?<br /><br />While there is still good story development, I did find some parts of the book were a bit slow. A good portion is dedicated to character and world building, however the book does not completely suffer from "first book syndrome" it does have its own beginning, middle and end, but I think the rest of the trilogy will be much more action packed with powerful plot twists.<br /><br />With this admirable debut, Amanda Hocking has begun a trilogy that has immense potential. Switched is just as beautiful inside as it is on the outside (definite cover lust) and I highly recommend it!<br /><br />--<br />For more of my reviews, visit my blog at <a href="http://www.xpressoreads.com" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <b>Xpresso Reads</b>
</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="15671671030383892962" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_1165672226" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1165672226" />
    <a title="Pearl Angeli" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/31514572-pearl-angeli"><img alt="Pearl Angeli" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1588420465p2/31514572.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1165672226?book_show_action=true">Jan 12, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Pearl Angeli" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Pearl Angeli" href="/user/show/31514572-pearl-angeli">Pearl Angeli</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781447205692" href="/book/show/12133821-switched">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31514572-pearl-angeli?shelf=owned-physical-copy">owned-physical-copy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31514572-pearl-angeli?shelf=young-adult-fantasy">young-adult-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31514572-pearl-angeli?shelf=series-completed">series-completed</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31514572-pearl-angeli?shelf=2015-reads">2015-reads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31514572-pearl-angeli?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1165672226" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6987469991028559151">First off, <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/8564935.Switched__Trylle___1_' title='Switched (Trylle, #1) by Amanda Hocking' rel='nofollow noopener'>Switched</a> is really gorgeous. Just look at the cover. Isn't it so beautiful? I personally chose this edition because the cover has some work of <i>magic</i> in it. It's like, it has an ability to suck me into its world. Beautiful!<br/><br/>Second, the premise is really, really good. I love fae stories, and <b>trolls</b> are something new to me. I wanted to know more about trolls because I really find them interesting. <br/><br/>And of course, the fact that the female character <b>Wendy Everly</b> is a troll and a <i>changeling</i>, </span>
  <span id="freeText6987469991028559151" style="display:none">First off, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/8564935.Switched__Trylle___1_" title="Switched (Trylle, #1) by Amanda Hocking" rel="nofollow noopener">Switched</a> is really gorgeous. Just look at the cover. Isn't it so beautiful? I personally chose this edition because the cover has some work of <i>magic</i> in it. It's like, it has an ability to suck me into its world. Beautiful!<br><br>Second, the premise is really, really good. I love fae stories, and <b>trolls</b> are something new to me. I wanted to know more about trolls because I really find them interesting. <br><br>And of course, the fact that the female character <b>Wendy Everly</b> is a troll and a <i>changeling</i>, I knew I will really like this book.<br><br><b>So, was this book a yay or nay?</b><br><br>I must say, a little bit of both.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1391193596ra/8345252.gif" width="350" height="250" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I love it because honestly, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/3486415.Amanda_Hocking" title="Amanda Hocking" rel="nofollow noopener">Amanda Hocking</a>'s writing style is so flawless and very easy to read. She uses words that are light and undemanding. She doesn't complicate everything and she doesn't give me trouble analyzing such things. Her <b>character and world-building</b> is also non-complex. What you read is what you get. <br><br>Now what made me become (a little) bit disappointed was the <b>plot</b>. It was neatly done, but it was weak. The progression was poorly established. I think there were scenes that weren't really necessary but they were given emphasis (I guess to lengthen the whole book) but to be honest, the interesting things only happened at the last few chapters of the book. <br><br>Another thing that bothered me was the existence of the <b>Vittras</b>. These are the creatures that act as antagonists. They are Trylle's greatest enemies. In this book, their descriptions unfortunately didn't make an exceptional appeal. Their physicality was so vague. I couldn't really imagine how they look like. Do they look like human or something?<br><br>My expectation for this book was also different. Because this book talks about trolls, I really expected to see some unworldly mythical creatures here. Creatures that look like these:<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1444376529i/16493140._SY540_.jpg" width="250" height="350" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1444376593i/16493145.jpg" width="250" height="350" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1444376664i/16493149.jpg" width="250" height="250" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Because we're talking about trolls, right? <br><br>So why did I only see humans and no trolls at all? This is fantasy so I was looking for something different. Anyway, I understand it as I've read further, because the author eventually explained it through her characters that trolls don't really look mystical but instead, they look human. So yeah, I couldn't do anything about that. BUT STILL. I want to see <b>REAL TROLLS</b>. :-/<br><br>Nevertheless, the thing that absolutely lifted the whole story was <b>Finn</b>. This character is so amazing. I like him from the beginning up to the end. Even though he's brooding and he was quite snobby in most parts of the book, the gentleness and protectiveness in him were so tangible. <br><br>I have nothing against Wendy, on the other hand. She's an okay character and she doesn't annoy me, but I think she needs some <b>development</b>. There were parts when she doesn't know what to do and she's very dependent to other people despite her extraordinary abilities. Hopefully her character will get better in the next books.<br><br>As a whole, this book is good. I just think it needs more elements to make it really sensational. My friends who have already read this series told me that it's going to get better in the next installments, so we'll see. Good luck to me! (oh, it rhymes! ha!)<br><br>Rating: 3 Stars</span>
  <a data-text-id="6987469991028559151" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer10320521070972314085">Review also posted on my <a href='https://edwardsghostengine.wordpress.com/2017/09/22/switched-amanda-hocking/#more-3729' rel='nofollow noopener'>blog.</a><br/><br/>I finished this awhile ago and am quite glad I decided to do so. There are plenty of suspenseful moments in this book which is why I kept reading bu there are also things lacking. <br/><br/>One thing that got on my nerves was the lack of character building. I mean nearly all the characters felt like cardboard cutouts with no depth or personality. I found them hard to emphasise with. And another hing is I would have liked to know a bit more about the trolls themselves and what</span>
  <span id="freeText10320521070972314085" style="display:none">Review also posted on my <a href="https://edwardsghostengine.wordpress.com/2017/09/22/switched-amanda-hocking/#more-3729" rel="nofollow noopener">blog.</a><br /><br />I finished this awhile ago and am quite glad I decided to do so. There are plenty of suspenseful moments in this book which is why I kept reading bu there are also things lacking. <br /><br />One thing that got on my nerves was the lack of character building. I mean nearly all the characters felt like cardboard cutouts with no depth or personality. I found them hard to emphasise with. And another hing is I would have liked to know a bit more about the trolls themselves and what I is exactly that makes them more special than humans? I mean yeah they have magical powers that have been diluted over time and they "commune with the earth" don't like to wear shoes and sometimes have a greenish tinge but that's about all that's described oh and they leave their babies as changelings in rich families so that the rest of the trylle can have the money for medical care and a comfortable life when the channelling returns to the community.<br /><br />Another thing that bothered me was than Wendy HARDLY EVER stood up for herself when her mother treated her like shit and everyone else around her just expected her to know everything about trylle culture and forget about her home life. I was so frustrated at times I wanted to reach into the book and shake some sense into her. I just hope she becomes stronger in later books.<br /><br />I also would have liked to learn more about he vittra and why they are a violent sect of trolls and exactly what they want as this was unclear. But overall a good even read and a series I will continue in time.</span>

<div id="review_152692386" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/152692386" />
    <a title="Limonessa" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4147373-limonessa"><img alt="Limonessa" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1424025988p2/4147373.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/152692386?book_show_action=true">Mar 07, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Limonessa" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Limonessa" href="/user/show/4147373-limonessa">Limonessa</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781453688939" href="/book/show/8564935-switched">review of another edition</a>

          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">the author to work more on it</span></div>

          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Limonessa by: </span>
      <a href="/user/show/4547586-vasya">Vasya</a>
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4147373-limonessa?shelf=ebook">ebook</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4147373-limonessa?shelf=ya-lit">ya-lit</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4147373-limonessa?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4147373-limonessa?shelf=paranormal-ya">paranormal-ya</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer152692386" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12316763893171288393">Well, this was interesting. <br/>I've read and heard some much about Amanda Hocking lately - even an article on a major Italian newspaper - that I finally decided to give it a try. <br/>I'd like to start by saying that this is my second attempt at a self published author and the first one didn't go well. The other book I read was <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/4908510.Almost_Human___The_First_Trilogy___3_in_1_Bundle' title='Almost Human ~ The First Trilogy ~ 3-in-1 Bundle by Melanie Nowak' rel='nofollow noopener'>ALMOST HUMAN ~ The First Trilogy ~ 3-in-1 Edition</a> and the main problem with it was the editing. The book was probably 150 pages longer than necessary and there was so much intern</span>
  <span id="freeText12316763893171288393" style="display:none">Well, this was interesting. <br />I've read and heard some much about Amanda Hocking lately - even an article on a major Italian newspaper - that I finally decided to give it a try. <br />I'd like to start by saying that this is my second attempt at a self published author and the first one didn't go well. The other book I read was <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/4908510.Almost_Human___The_First_Trilogy___3_in_1_Bundle" title="Almost Human ~ The First Trilogy ~ 3-in-1 Bundle by Melanie Nowak" rel="nofollow noopener">ALMOST HUMAN ~ The First Trilogy ~ 3-in-1 Edition</a> and the main problem with it was the editing. The book was probably 150 pages longer than necessary and there was so much internal monologue that I skipped and skipped and skipped.<br /><br />With Switched the fundamental problem is basically the same: editing. This book is better than the one I mentioned above but it still needs a professional hand working through it. It certainly does not need to be cut. On the contrary. It jumped from action to action to action without any character development at all. Wendy goes from finding Finn creepy to falling in love with him without maturing the feeling inside her at all. BAM! I've fallen for him. <br />The dialogue is horrific at times, there are long parts where the characters are just bickering and repeating things over and over.<br /><br />The second part of the book was definitely better than the first. The writing flowed better, even the dialogue got better and I almost never "furrowed my brow" like the characters so many times did. I was kind of shocked at the end when the escape scene is described in approximately 20 lines. It felt like Hocking was tired of writing or had finished her word count for the day and decided to cut it short. <br /><br />Plotwise once again I can't really say this book was anything new or original. I appreciated the Troll theme - that is new - but the rest is pretty much standard in YA lit now. Finn, especially, reminded me of a mix of Patch from <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6339664.Hush__Hush__Hush__Hush___1_" title="Hush, Hush (Hush, Hush, #1) by Becca Fitzpatrick" rel="nofollow noopener">Hush Hush</a> (the stalking) and Sonny from <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/3064985.Wondrous_Strange__Wondrous_Strange___1_" title="Wondrous Strange (Wondrous Strange, #1) by Lesley Livingston" rel="nofollow noopener">Wondrous Strange</a>. <br />Wendy I didn't like AT ALL. What a pain in the ass she is. She kind of sounds like a badass at the beginning and then she turns in this whiny, please-Finn-save-me thing. Tove and Rhys I liked, especially Tove, an interesting character with a lot of potential. Matt is a totally underdeveloped character and i'm guessing we'll see more of him in the next installment.<br /><br />All in all, I can say this book was OK. Considering it is self published it is even good. But I also think that Hocking needs to mature as a writer, get published and acquire some new ideas. I will be looking for her work in a few years time.</span>
  <a data-text-id="12316763893171288393" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_165527323" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/165527323" />
    <a title="Shannon" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/73981-shannon"><img alt="Shannon" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1263059140p2/73981.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/165527323?book_show_action=true">May 04, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Shannon" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Shannon" href="/user/show/73981-shannon">Shannon</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781453688939" href="/book/show/8564935-switched">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/73981-shannon?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/73981-shannon?shelf=ya">ya</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer165527323" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3528471642199176742">*Sigh*<br/><br/>So I went into this with low expectations. I had heard that the books were riddled with typos, so on and etc. But I made the argument to myself that most people do. "It's only $0.99."<br/><br/>What I liked... 1. good pacing. The books have a zip-zip pace to them, and I think that's what draws a lot of people in. 2. There is a sense of playfulness. <br/><br/>What I didn't like. <br/><br/>1. Trolls... treillings, whatever you call them. Just, really? I just couldn't get beyond the image in my head from a Merlin episode w</span>
  <span id="freeText3528471642199176742" style="display:none">*Sigh*<br /><br />So I went into this with low expectations. I had heard that the books were riddled with typos, so on and etc. But I made the argument to myself that most people do. "It's only $0.99."<br /><br />What I liked... 1. good pacing. The books have a zip-zip pace to them, and I think that's what draws a lot of people in. 2. There is a sense of playfulness. <br /><br />What I didn't like. <br /><br />1. Trolls... treillings, whatever you call them. Just, really? I just couldn't get beyond the image in my head from a Merlin episode where a troll posing as a queen seduces Uther and spends most of the episode eating rotten produce. Just ew. And there wasn't really an effort made (besides the snooty name change offered by the troll-mom) to adjust the reader.<br /><br />2. The typos. But meh, not the end of the world.<br /><br />3. The total inconsistency of the plot. The human brother is real the heroine. And the mom trying to kill the troll daughter... um, in a different story it would be completely justifiable and she would be the protagonist. Like, you have to suspend a great deal of brain power to be like "okay, losing your son wouldn't make you crazy..." because I think it would.<br /><br />4. The reason for the switching... is disgusting. For money? Really? REALLY? That's the only reason. At the cost of a human child being separated from their family... I couldn't get over that. <br /><br />Finally, a lot of this would be justifiable if the writing was more complex or had just "a bit more." But I think these books are representative of works too quickly written. <br /><br />Sigh, I wanted to like these more, but I can't recommend that anyone else read them when compared to the whole slew of books on the market that are bettered edited and written with more care. Overall, I'd give this book more like a 1.5, but I have zero desire to read the rest.</span>
  <a data-text-id="3528471642199176742" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5691412-megs?shelf=z-2011-reads">z-2011-reads</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">

<span id="freeTextContainer1198030055957874029">Ugghh! I like Amanda Hocking. I loved her series <i>My Blood Approves</i>, but this book was disappointing. <br/><br/>Originally I tried to read this when it was first self published, and couldn't finish it. I got about halfway, put it down, thinking I have way too many better things to be reading right now than this troll book. It wasn't even like I hated it, I just got incredibly bored and got to a point where realized I didn't care about Wendy or what happens to her. <br/><br/>So we know that recently it was republishe</span>
  <span id="freeText1198030055957874029" style="display:none">Ugghh! I like Amanda Hocking. I loved her series <i>My Blood Approves</i>, but this book was disappointing. <br /><br />Originally I tried to read this when it was first self published, and couldn't finish it. I got about halfway, put it down, thinking I have way too many better things to be reading right now than this troll book. It wasn't even like I hated it, I just got incredibly bored and got to a point where realized I didn't care about Wendy or what happens to her. <br /><br />So we know that recently it was republished and a lot of my friends have rated this book in the 4-5 star range so I began to wonder if I was missing something. I was also prompted to try the repubbed version because it was supposedly polished up a bit, and so I gave it another try. <br /><br />Well, that was stupid. I should have just trusted my instincts and known that just because so many other people enjoyed this book didn't mean I would magically change my mind about it. Also, I'm really happy for Amanda and all of her success so I just really <i>wanted</i> to like this series.<br /><br />I'm not going to go into too much detail about the things I liked or didn't like, because there are a large amount of points already made for both, but as a simple short list the things I didn't like were: Wendy, Wendy's Mom, the dialog What I liked was: Flynn, the originality of the story and the changeling aspect. The world was creative, but the story and characters didn't offer much. The synopsis really made this book seem interesting, too. Oh well.<br /><br />To those who love this series I would like to know why. This book didn't "suck me in" from the beginning, or even by halfway. </span>

<div id="review_1834930995" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1834930995" />
    <a title="Kaylin (The Re-Read Queen)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/47627265-kaylin-the-re-read-queen"><img alt="Kaylin (The Re-Read Queen)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1560356189p2/47627265.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1834930995?book_show_action=true">Mar 16, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kaylin (The Re-Read Queen)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kaylin (The Re-Read Queen)" href="/user/show/47627265-kaylin-the-re-read-queen">Kaylin (The Re-Read Queen)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/47627265-kaylin-the-re-read-queen?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/47627265-kaylin-the-re-read-queen?shelf=paranormal">paranormal</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/47627265-kaylin-the-re-read-queen?shelf=finished-but-wish-i-hadn-t">finished-but-wish-i-hadn-t</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1834930995" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8079407655856705479"><b> 2 Stars<br/><br/>Overview: </b><br/><br/><i>
  <blockquote>“Did you think you could treat me like shit at a dance, then sneak into my room in the middle of the night and tell me that I'm a troll with magical powers, and I'd just be like, yeah, that sounds right.”</blockquote>
</i><br/><br/>So trolls<br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1489772882i/22248692._SX540_.png' width='400' height='200' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>Only not those.<br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1489772882ra/22248693.gif' width='400' height='198' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>And not those. <br/><br/>Instead:<br/>Wendy has spent her entire life feeling as if she does not belong. Her mother attempted to kill her when she was six-years-old, claiming she was a “monster,” and since that time, Wendy has moved from place to place with her lov</span>
  <span id="freeText8079407655856705479" style="display:none"><b> 2 Stars<br><br>Overview: </b><br><br><i>
  <blockquote>“Did you think you could treat me like shit at a dance, then sneak into my room in the middle of the night and tell me that I'm a troll with magical powers, and I'd just be like, yeah, that sounds right.”</blockquote>
</i><br><br>So trolls<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1489772882i/22248692._SX540_.png" width="400" height="200" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Only not those.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1489772882ra/22248693.gif" width="400" height="198" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>And not those. <br><br>Instead:<br>Wendy has spent her entire life feeling as if she does not belong. Her mother attempted to kill her when she was six-years-old, claiming she was a “monster,” and since that time, Wendy has moved from place to place with her loving brother and aunt. Until she moves to a new school and meets a mysterious new boy with a striking eye color (black) and a penchant for climbing in her windows at night, who dutifully informs her that she is actually a troll who was switched at birth. <br><br>Remember 2008-2009? When Beyonce first let us know that if we liked it we should have put a ring on it and Britney repeatedly told us what she thought of womanizers. Michael Jackson died and Obama was elected US president.<br><br>This is also when Twilight became super popular and there was this <i>surge</i> of Paranormal YA. This was initially published in 2010 on the heels of this, and out of that wave of paranormal books this <i>does</i> stand out. It is fairly original, has a fun premise and moves quickly. If I’d read this back then, I probably would have enjoyed it. But looking at it now, it’s just a string of paranormal clichés<br><br><b>Pros:</b><br><br>Like I said, this <i>is</i> fairly original in some aspects. The overall ideas about trolls (or Trylle, as Wendy’s ‘tribe’ is called) and changelings are very well thought out and creative. <br><br>The pacing in this was great! It moved very quickly without being confusing and it was very much a short, action-infused read.<br><br>Yay for MC calling love-interest out when his staring is creepy. <br><br><b>Cons:</b><br><br>Alllllll the clichés:<br>-	“I’ve never fit in anywhere!”<br>-	Mysterious new boy with ‘striking’ eyes. <br>-	He’s climbin’ in yo windows<br>-	The lost princess!<br>-	Insta-love<br>-	With hints of a love triangle!<br>-	“My hair is so wild and my eyes are so plain but everyone who sees me is in awe of my beauty!”<br><br>Okay, but Wendy’s brother really freaked me out. He’s portrayed as a ‘loving, but protective’ sibling, but what he actually does is scream at Wendy when she does something he doesn’t approve of and threatens to “kill everyone at the dance” for upsetting her. <i>This is not okay. </i><br><br>I understand Wendy’s relationship with her ‘mother’ is complicated, but she kept flip-flopping. One paragraph she would call her a “good mother” and the next say she was a horrible woman who only ever attempted to murder her. This was never really addressed in any nuanced way, only Wendy making alternating exclamations. <br><br><b>In Conclusion: </b><br><br>A fairly original idea that gets bogged down with clichés. </span>
  <a data-text-id="8079407655856705479" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_2365461279" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2365461279" />
    <a title="Sarah" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/45261627-sarah"><img alt="Sarah" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1475352701p2/45261627.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2365461279?book_show_action=true">Apr 19, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sarah" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sarah" href="/user/show/45261627-sarah">Sarah</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781250006318" href="/book/show/11457525-switched">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/45261627-sarah?shelf=almost-gothic-in-a-natural-way">almost-gothic-in-a-natural-way</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/45261627-sarah?shelf=blue-eyed-male-entity">blue-eyed-male-entity</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/45261627-sarah?shelf=at-my-library">at-my-library</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/45261627-sarah?shelf=dark-eyed-male-entity">dark-eyed-male-entity</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/45261627-sarah?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/45261627-sarah?shelf=kings-and-queens">kings-and-queens</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/45261627-sarah?shelf=pretty-red-cover">pretty-red-cover</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/45261627-sarah?shelf=urban-fantasy">urban-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/45261627-sarah?shelf=red-blue-green-covers">red-blue-green-covers</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/45261627-sarah?shelf=because-magic">because-magic</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2365461279" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3538145651324413215"><i>Switched</i> begins with a flashback. Our narrator, a seventeen-year-old named Wendy Everly, tells us the occasion that she first became aware that she was a “monster.” She was six years old and throwing a tantrum at her own perfectly nice birthday party. But we can’t quite dismiss little Wendy as nothing but a brat, because her father died very shortly before her birthday.<br/> <br/>Wendy storms back to the kitchen to yell at her mother for buying her a chocolate cake when Mommy knows full well that Wendy do</span>
  <span id="freeText3538145651324413215" style="display:none"><i>Switched</i> begins with a flashback. Our narrator, a seventeen-year-old named Wendy Everly, tells us the occasion that she first became aware that she was a “monster.” She was six years old and throwing a tantrum at her own perfectly nice birthday party. But we can’t quite dismiss little Wendy as nothing but a brat, because her father died very shortly before her birthday.<br> <br>Wendy storms back to the kitchen to yell at her mother for buying her a chocolate cake when Mommy knows full well that Wendy doesn’t like chocolate—this is the reader’s first major clue that something’s wrong with Wendy. For this, the spoiled child deserves perhaps to be sent to bed early, lose dessert privileges, or get bopped on the head with a rolled-up newspaper. <br><br>But no, Wendy’s mother declares that the little girl is a monster and no offspring of hers. She stabs at Wendy erratically with a large knife, and probably would have killed her had not eleven-year-old Matt, her biological son, stepped in just there. As is, Wendy has a giant scar on her stomach that will stay forever.<br><br>Fast-forward eleven years. Matt and Wendy live with their aunt Maggie, their mother having been institutionalized shortly after the knife incident. Matt has done all right for himself, but Wendy has bombed out of several public schools, and has a rep for being sullen, difficult and rather stupid, all of which is true.<br> <br>There’s a boy in one of Wendy’s classes who stares at her. He has black hair and pale skin and beautiful dark eyes, and his name is Finn. On the day our story begins, Wendy decides to ask him why he stares. “Everyone stares at you,” he replies with no visible emotion. “You’re very attractive.” He’s a lot like every other sulky, leather-jacket-wearing, late 2000s paranormal YA love interest, but unlike Edward Cullen or Jace Wayland, Finn just spits it right out. Credit where credit is due.<br><br>Why is he named Finn, though? A guy named Finn is almost always a wholesome character. He’s supposed to be a farm boy who shelters fugitive princesses and wears the sweaters his momma knitted for him, or a former Stormtrooper with a heart full of empathy for Resistance pilots, scavenger orphans, mechanics, and space goats. Same goes for a lad named Ben, James, Sam, or Will. The emotionally-unavailable bad boy with a hidden heart of gold archetype is more likely to be named something like Nick or Jack. <br><br>Finn also tells Wendy that he’s noticed her ability to think something at someone and make them change their mind. She has always been able to do this—say, she looks at an angry teacher and thinks “You aren’t going to send me to the principal” and the teacher, a bit befuddled, sits down and tells her “You don’t have to go to the principal’s office.” Sometimes she wonders if this is what her mom meant about her being a monster. At any rate, it frightens her that Finn (or anyone, for that matter) knows of this talent of hers.<br><br>She uses this talent to persuade Matt, who knows better and is very worried, to drive her to the asylum for an audience with their mom. Wendy interrogates the woman but comes away with little she didn’t already know. Her mother raves that Wendy, as a baby, somehow disposed of Michael, the mother’s biological second son, and substituted herself. Matt dismisses this as the ranting of a lunatic but his sister thinks there might be some truth to it.<br><br>Wendy goes to the school dance for the first time ever, solely to talk with Finn some more, but he says something callous, she becomes enraged, and she hurriedly leaves before he can explain. Good thing he just decided to climb through her bedroom window and explain it to her anyway. This is one of a few spots where the book treads a little too close to <i>Twilight</i>, although given the changeling theme, it could also be a nod to <i>Peter Pan</i> (our heroine’s name is Wendy, after all) or <i>Labyrinth</i> (albeit Jareth is much, much cooler than Finn).<br><br>Did I say changeling? Turns out that Wendy is not only adopted, she’s not even technically human. She belongs to a race of creatures from Norse folklore called the Trylle—known to humans as trolls, but not to be confused with the monsters that live under bridges and/or eat jellied Dwarves. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1524921941ra/25447956.gif" width="500" height="200" alt="Trolls vs. Bilbo" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Nope, these trolls—er, Trylle—look human enough, although they’re prettier than most of us and might have a green undertone to their skin.<br><br>The Trylle culture is dying out. For the past several generations they have swapped their royal/high-ranking babies with human infants, so the Trylle babies can acquire wealth and education while in human society, then bring at least some of that back to their true people once they return. Finn is a Tracker, a low-ranking Trylle whose job is to find adolescent changelings and bring them home. And Wendy is the only daughter of the Trylle Queen, the inexorable Elora.<br><br>Finn wants Wendy to come to the hidden Trylle stronghold in Minnesota with him, but she hedges, thinking of the worry she’d cause her aunt and especially her brother. Then she gets attacked by a rival band of Trylle, called the Vittra, and realizes she endangers her human family if she stays…<br><br><b>Content Advisory</b><br><i>Violence</i>: Stylized, action-movie style fights between the Trylle and the Vittra. Very little actual weaponry used. Lots of punching and flying through windows. No gorier than the average Rick Riordan book.<br><br><i>Sex</i>: Finn and Wendy make out a few times, despite not knowing each other well at all. The night before he has to leave the settlement, he spends snuggling in bed with her—snuggling is all they do. Before that, she suspected that her mother had a creepy, Mrs. Robinson-like relationship with him; in reality, <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Elora had been in love with Finn’s father and had some sort of maternal feeling for him, which she squelched as soon as she realized he liked her daughter and was a threat to the Trylle aristocracy. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> Elora is currently having an affair with a Trylle lord, the father of one of Wendy’s new friends, which is thankfully not shown in any detail.<br><br>Rhys invites Wendy to join him for a <i>Lord of the Rings</i> marathon and she falls asleep on his couch. Finn gets there and assumes the absolute worst, despite a lack of any real evidence.<br><br><i>Language</i>: There’s one F-bomb and a variety of less pungent four-letter words in here.<br> <br><i>Substance Abuse</i>: Social champagne drinking, including by the underage and very awkward Wendy. <br><br><i>Nightmare Fuel</i>: Nothing.<br> <br><i>Politics and Religion</i>: Nothing.<br><br><b>Conclusion</b><br><i>Switched</i> is definitely part of the post-<i>Twilight</i> paranormal trend: awkward brown-haired heroine, sulky love interest with no concept of personal space, glamorous hidden society in some rural part of America….too much melodrama for a story that just started and characters we barely know, and prose that veers from fine to patchy.<br><br>This paperback edition includes four bonus chapters called “The Vittra Attack.” The publisher labels this a short story but it isn’t—it has no arc of its own and is hard to follow until you finally see where it connects to the main body of the story. These four chapters are from the POV of a Vittra named Loki, whom I assure you I was not picturing as Tom Hiddleston with long black hair. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1524921941ra/25447957.gif" width="400" height="237" alt="Loki laughing" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br>Ahem. Loki drives the getaway car for the two Vittra who tried to capture Wendy. He gets pushed around by the Vittra king, but is close to their queen, for some reason. Loki is never shown or mentioned in the book proper, so I don’t know why Hocking considered him important enough for his own bonus chapters. At any rate, the book would have been improved if his chapters were woven into the main book—it would have added at least <i>some</i> sense of urgency.<br><br>It’s silly, fast-paced, not terribly deep, and enjoyable enough that I’ll probably read the second book. It’s a good deal better than the aforementioned Twilight Saga or the Mortal Instruments series, but not nearly as much fun as the Percy Jackson books.<br><br>If you want a melodramatic YA urban fantasy trilogy that’s actually mostly <i>good</i>, though, check out A.G. Howard’s Splintered trilogy. It has one very annoying major character, but the prose and worldbuilding are solid. </["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>
  <a data-text-id="3538145651324413215" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

    <a title="Ivana - Diary of Difference" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/28198445-ivana---diary-of-difference"><img alt="Ivana - Diary of Difference" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1555964929p2/28198445.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2886475888?book_show_action=true">Mar 31, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ivana - Diary of Difference" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ivana - Diary of Difference" href="/user/show/28198445-ivana---diary-of-difference">Ivana - Diary of Difference</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2886475888" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11088848082131903657"><a href='https://amzn.to/2Wi7amb' rel='nofollow noopener'>Wishlist</a> | <a></a><a href='https://diaryofdifference.com/' rel='nofollow noopener'>Blog</a> | <a href='https://www.facebook.com/diaryofdifference/' rel='nofollow noopener'>Facebook</a> | <a href='https://twitter.com/DiaryDifference' rel='nofollow noopener'>Twitter</a> | <a href='https://www.instagram.com/diaryofdifference/' rel='nofollow noopener'>Instagram</a> | <a href='https://www.pinterest.co.uk/diaryofdifference/pins/' rel='nofollow noopener'>Pinterest</a><br/><br/>#1 <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2886475888' rel='nofollow noopener'>Switched</a> - ★★★★★<br/>#1 <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3257360720' rel='nofollow noopener'>Torn</a> - Not Read Yet<br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1585732762i/29210509._SX540_.png' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/><b>Wendy Everly knew she was different the day her mother tried to kill her…</b><br/><br/>Her mother told her she has been switched at birth. Unable to fit anywhere, bored and frustrated by her small-town life, she also has to hide her secret - the fact that she can somehow influence people’s decisions, without knowing how or why she does it.<br/><br/>When the dark and handsome Finn shows up at her bedroom window one night</span>
  <span id="freeText11088848082131903657" style="display:none"><a href="https://amzn.to/2Wi7amb" rel="nofollow noopener">Wishlist</a> | <a></a><a href="https://diaryofdifference.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog</a> | <a href="https://www.facebook.com/diaryofdifference/" rel="nofollow noopener">Facebook</a> | <a href="https://twitter.com/DiaryDifference" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> | <a href="https://www.instagram.com/diaryofdifference/" rel="nofollow noopener">Instagram</a> | <a href="https://www.pinterest.co.uk/diaryofdifference/pins/" rel="nofollow noopener">Pinterest</a><br><br>#1 <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2886475888" rel="nofollow noopener">Switched</a> - ★★★★★<br>#1 <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3257360720" rel="nofollow noopener">Torn</a> - Not Read Yet<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1585732762i/29210509._SX540_.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>Wendy Everly knew she was different the day her mother tried to kill her…</b><br><br>Her mother told her she has been switched at birth. Unable to fit anywhere, bored and frustrated by her small-town life, she also has to hide her secret - the fact that she can somehow influence people’s decisions, without knowing how or why she does it.<br><br>When the dark and handsome Finn shows up at her bedroom window one night, her life changes forever! The secret she has been waiting for has finally been revealed. Finn holds the key to her past and has an answer to her strange ability. He is also about to introduce her to a place she never imagined could exist: Forening, the home of Trylle.<br><br>Among the Trylle she is not different, but she is special. But being special also brings danger wherever she goes and with everything around her being new, Finn is the only person she can trust. But will trusting him be enough to stay alive?<br><br><a href="https://www.instagram.com/p/B-VtJ8ZAUlF/" rel="nofollow noopener">View this post on Instagram</a><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1585732762i/29210510.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>
  <i>My Thoughts:</i>
</b><br><br>I absolutely LOVED, LOVED, LOVED Switched, and I need to buy the second book in the series as soon as possible! <br><br>Wendy is a girl that you immediately want to be friends with. Witty, honest and caring, willing to do everything for the people she loves - she is so precious and I wouldn’t let anyone touch her!<br><br>Finn - he is the fiction version of my boyfriend… Dark, handsome, brutally honest and his ego can sometimes get in the way. He is a tracker - and his job is to find other people like Wendy, who have special powers. Finn is a sort of a body-guard. And because Wendy is special and the future Queen, she cannot be with anyone that is not the same or similar rank as her. Which means that being with Finn is impossible.<br><br><b>Not allowed.</b><br><br>Frowned upon and could result in banishment for both. Loss of crown type of bad. <br><br>From the first chapter I was into Wendy’s world and this book was so quick to read. I read it in less than a day and it felt too short! It’s a page-turner in every sense of the world. <br><br>The world building as well as the Trylle people were quite interesting and unique. I also loved the fact that even though Wendy and Finn were amazing characters, we met so many other characters, who were also very well portrayed in their own way and all left a mark: Elora, Rhys, Matt, Tove, Rhiannon, Willa… All of them had their own uniqueness, and I can imagine how hard it can be to give life to so many characters in such a small book.<br><br>I rooted for Wendy and Finn’s romance, as you can imagine, and I have to say, I was a bit disappointed with the ending. However, I knew that was the right choice for Wendy at the time, and also, it left a great cliff-hanger for the second book, for me to read. I think that in the second book, a few old things will open up again and maybe, this time, the ending will go as I wanted it to go in the first book. <br><br><b>
  <i>I recommend this book with all my heart to all of you that love fantasy and young-adult romance. You will read it fast and you will fall in love with it even faster. Switched is definitely a book I am adding to my favorites.</i>
</b><br><br><a href="https://amzn.to/2Wi7amb" rel="nofollow noopener">Wishlist</a> | <a></a><a href="https://diaryofdifference.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog</a> | <a href="https://www.facebook.com/diaryofdifference/" rel="nofollow noopener">Facebook</a> | <a href="https://twitter.com/DiaryDifference" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> | <a href="https://www.instagram.com/diaryofdifference/" rel="nofollow noopener">Instagram</a> | <a href="https://www.pinterest.co.uk/diaryofdifference/pins/" rel="nofollow noopener">Pinterest</a></span>

<div id="review_146790825" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/146790825" />
    <a title="Scott Heaton" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4947298-scott-heaton"><img alt="Scott Heaton" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1327422577p2/4947298.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/146790825?book_show_action=true">Feb 08, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Scott Heaton" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Scott Heaton" href="/user/show/4947298-scott-heaton">Scott Heaton</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781453688939" href="/book/show/8564935-switched">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer146790825" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17163149959317935406">'Switched’ by Amanda Hocking caught my eye due to its high position on Amazon Kindle’s bestsellers and it’s awesome price of 99 cents. Without knowing a thing about the book other than the brief synopsis I read before I downloaded the story, and the overwhelming number of positive reviews, I figured it would be an awesome quick read.<br/><br/>‘Switched’ is about Wendy Everly, a girl who lives with her aunt and brother in an attempt to control the chaos of her life. Her mother, Kim, tried to kill her on he</span>
  <span id="freeText17163149959317935406" style="display:none">'Switched’ by Amanda Hocking caught my eye due to its high position on Amazon Kindle’s bestsellers and it’s awesome price of 99 cents. Without knowing a thing about the book other than the brief synopsis I read before I downloaded the story, and the overwhelming number of positive reviews, I figured it would be an awesome quick read.<br /><br />‘Switched’ is about Wendy Everly, a girl who lives with her aunt and brother in an attempt to control the chaos of her life. Her mother, Kim, tried to kill her on her 6th birthday, and since then her life has been a downward spiral of changing homes and failed friendships. Within this backdrop we discover that Wendy has some peculiar abilities, and is given an opportunity by a mysterious boy, Finn, to move once again to a new place where she can finally fit in. However, if she decides to make the move she will have to leave behind her brother and aunt, the only two people who have ever cared about her.<br /><br />I’ve only revealed the first 20 pages or so and it sounds like a decent story line right? However, once the story begins to progress you discover that it doesn’t go anywhere. The plot never advances, the characters are underdeveloped, the conversation is so far away from colloquial it seems as if the ‘speaker’ is rummaging through a thesaurus before deciding on each word choice, and the romantic elements in the story make you cringe with the overwhelming amount of cheesiness. I suppose if you’re into the new ‘supernatural teen romance’ genre that is emerging, this book could be for you. But for anyone that is not familiar with this genre, stay clear of this book. Wendy experiences ’0′ change throughout the book and the story ends literally and figuratively exactly where it began.<br /><br />I was astonished to see how many positive reviews this book received, and I understand that Hocking is not attempting to write a literary masterpiece that is applauded by college English professors, but to me, the story was barely enjoyable. My 99 cents would have been better spent on the ‘Fruit Ninja” app for my iPhone.<br /><br />On a bookshelf with 5 shelves… shelf 5 being the highest and best, it doesn’t even make it to the shelf.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="17163149959317935406" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>
